B00CRMWMZ0|3.0|From a production standpoint, Random Access Memories sounds phenomenal. It's music as a gourmet lollipop. Total ear candy. An audiophile's best friend. What more could one ask for? What indeed...<br /><br />First, how about something new? Daft Punk explored very similar sounds on their 2001 masterpiece \\"Discovery.\\" Back then, their shift from underground house and techno stylings to a vibrant hybrid of \\"uncool\\" sounds from 70's and 80's AM radio was not only novel, it took guts to pull off. Now, two proper albums and twelve years later, DP are falling backward rather than pushing their music forward. Even worse, what really sets RAM apart from Discovery is the extent to which it slavishly imitates its influences rather than forge something new and identifiably D-Punkian. If you're already stocked up on Chic and Earth, Wind & Fire records and still can't get enough of those grooves, by all means enjoy the feast that awaits you here. But if not, you're better off getting the originals rather than the comparably tame knock-offs. For instance, \\"Get Lucky\\" and \\"Lose Yourself to Dance\\" both feature some classic funky licks from Chic's Nile Rogers, not to mention singer Pharrell Williams' best impersonation of EW&F. The songs are close to being a perfect fusion of the two bands, and yet Pharrell's voice sounds thin and forced compared to the smooth disco legends of yore, and his lyrics are just embarrassing. Plus, nowhere in the songs do the personality of its creators (remember, Daft Punk?) really pop out. Discovery is more than a decade old now, and it still sounds fresher than this one. So does \\"Moon Safari,\\" the 1998 album by Air. You know, that other French electronic duo who fused M.O.R. music from similar eras into a sound that the loungier tracks of R.A.M. come very close to duplicating---but alas, not quite.<br /><br />Second, how about something with a little more life to it? Even if you just want to ape your childhood heroes, at least do it with abandon. With the exception of the slightly more outr&eacute; narrative compositions \\"Giorgio on Moroder\\" and \\"Touch,\\" so much of this record feels safe, predictable, over-calculated, and bloodless. The lyrics are mind-numbingly superficial, just clich&eacute;d disco or ballad boilerplate. Don't get me wrong, Homework and Discovery weren't deep either, but their mish-mash of styles were darn inspired, often transcendent. By comparison, this can be ponderous, stodgy, even a bit preachy in its promotion of pop's past. Judging from the promotional features, it seemed as if Daft Punk were nursing some high ambitions with this record, and yet it's the most conservative thing I've heard in some time. Worse, it's completely guarded: these fuddy-duddies hiding in Robo helmets have obscured their own personalities within their perfected replication of bygone eras.  Kraftwerk sounds more expressive than this, and they were trying really hard to keep the robot thing up! Bangalter and de Homem-Christo, on the other hand, obsessing over the sonic details of their musical wax museum, have left all of the human touches to their guests. Ultimately, the Robots only care to give us a well-crafted dance \\"product,\\" a rich gourmet lollipop (with authentic nostalgia flavor!), a classy alternative to Skrillex, and hope we don't crave something more substantial.<br /><br />Some will be perfectly fine with this luxury confection. They'll eat it up without a second thought. Me, I'll pare this down to the eight best songs (i.e., the ones that aren't completely boring), and have a grooving, non-intrusive soundtrack to spreadsheet maintenance and household chores. 193700788X|1.0|[warning - spoilers] I have been a big fan of the Sookie Stackhouse series and have not submitted a negative comment on a book before. However, Dead Ever After was so poorly thought out and written as a final chapter to a great series that I felt I had to.  If I could give this book a negative 10 score, I would.  All of the characters created by CH have become three- dimensional for me and I am not a committed supporter of Eric, Bill or Sam as Sookie's HEA. I can even accept CH's choice of Sam for Sookie, since it is hard to think of Eric or Bill as Sookie's \\"soul-mate\\" or \\"life partner\\", being vampires (and quite dead). However, if CH wanted to conclude the series with Sookie choosing Sam, she chose a very strange way of doing it. After Sookie saves Sam's life with the cluviel dor, Sam is reclusive and appears ungrateful to Sookie for saving his life. Then, when Sookie is put in jail, Sam agrees to Eric's demand that he have no contact with Sookie if Eric will post Sookie's bail. Sam comes off as a beta male, with Eric staying the alpha male. Sam bargains away his right to pursue Sookie for just $30,000. Pretty pathetic excuse for a man!<br /><br />I also am appalled at the way CH trashed Eric in DEA. He did not deserve that treatment, since his meekly accepting bondage to Freyda and suggesting that Sookie follow him to Oklahoma to be a hidden mistress is totally out of character for him. Also, Bill deserved one last chance to redeem himself in Sookie's eyes. Rather than mope about Sookie not ending up with either Eric or Bill (or Alcide) in subsequent negative comments posted on the book, I think it would be great if other fans could suggest plot lines for DEA that could have established Sam as being worthy of Sookie. After all, since CH created the Sookie Stackhouse world, it is her right to decide who Sookie ends up with. Besides being an interesting project, it would serve an additional purpose of establishing how easy it would have been for CH to honor her fans by thinking up a story line that allowed Sookie to end up with Sam in a convincing manner, while still providing a dignified and honorable exit for Eric and Bill. This would then help explain why so many fans feel that DEA was an insult inflicted on the loyal readers (and a particularly nasty insult directed at Eric fans).<br /><br />For example, why not have the cluviel dor change Sam, so that he awoke from death energized, grateful to Sookie and realizing that she must truly love him in order to sacrifice her one magic wish on him instead of on Eric. Instead of changing into a collie, Sam could start changing into a Bengal tiger in order to emphasize his newly found alpha male personality (and maybe even kill some of King Felipe's vampires to save Sookie's life in the middle of the book).<br /><br />Instead of the nonsense about the devil, Copley Carmichael and Claude, the focal point of DEA could have been the resolution of how Eric schemes to get out of his bondage to Freyda and keep Sookie, even though forced at the beginning of the book to dissolve his marriage to Sookie.  Sookie could agonize over her established love for Eric and her new attraction to Sam, who has been changed by the cluviel dor and who is actively pursuing Sookie. Perhaps Bill could have discovered some loophole due to his vampire genealogical research that could ultimately be used by Eric to break his bondage to Freyda. Freyda and Felipe de Castro do not accept this outcome and Bill, Eric, Sookie and Sam battle Felipe and Freyda in a final epic battle. Bill dies in the battle in order to save Sookie (redeeming himself and dying in Sookie's arms), but Sookie, Eric and Sam are left standing at the end. Sam (shapeshifted into a Bengal tiger) proves his worth as a warrior at Eric's side during the battle.  At the end of this DEA, Eric realizes that if he truly loves Sookie, he needs to leave in order for Sam to provide Sookie with the happy ending (and family) that she deserves. Having killed Felipe de Castro, Eric becomes the King of Nevada, Arkansas and Louisiana, moves to New Orleans, and leaves Pam in charge as the local Sheriff.<br /><br />In my ideal DEA that CH could have written, at the end of the book Sookie and Sam are sitting on the porch of her house drinking lemonade. There is a full moon out that night and a tapestry of stars shine overhead. The scent of lilacs surrounds the house. Bubba has moved into Bill's house and is in the cemetery singing a song of lost love and new love found. The Weres can be heard in the deep woods howling as they hunt. The sealed fae portal can be seen in the distance shimmering slightly, a faint line of changing colors, shifting in resonance to Bubba's song. The effect of the cluviel dor is that Sookie sometimes hears Sam's thoughts and sometimes not, but she has found that when she does hear his thoughts, she doesn't mind at all, because she almost always likes what he is thinking. On the porch that night, she hears him worry about whether their children will have a difficult life being part fae and part shapeshifter. Sookie reassures him that she has learned one thing living all these years in Bon Temps. The world is a strange and dangerous, but beautiful place - and sometimes you have to accept the strangeness in you, because what may be strange and not \\"normal\\" may be the one thing that helps you survive in this crazy world.<br /><br />I am not an author, but I imagine there are other fans who have the talent to think up a fitting plot line for DEA that would have served CH's purpose better than the truly awful drivel she served up in DEA. Give it a try and post your ideas!<br /><br />UPDATE:<br /><br />One SVM fan has accepted the challenge and has come up with their own alternate ending to DEA:<br /><br />http://whatisafterdea.wordpress.com/

Ragnar is sharp, cunning, and always wears an evil grin while his priest slave is contemplative, weak, and innocent. Ragnar's wife obliges, going so far as to show a little thigh to the chaste young friar. The writers of Vikings did an excellent job as the script is clear, precise, and injects action at just the right points. It can be slow, but it's not convoluted like Robert Jordan's televised slogfest. There are no colliding characters with their own separate plot lines to worry about; this is Ragnar Lothbrok's show. B00C061I3K|5.0|Daft Punk's fourth studio album proper has got to be the most anticipated album so far this year. It far exceeds the hype; Disco, Funk, and Rock with a human feel. Most of the instrumentation is real with Nile Rodgers scratchy funky guitars, and other guests like Pharrell, Julian Casablancas, Paul Williams, Todd Edwards, Panda Bear, and the legendary Giorgio Moroder who appears on \\"Giorgio By Moroder\\" narrating his earlier career in Germany (and particularly his work on Donna Summer's ground breaking \\"I Remember Yesterday\\" album\\" which incorporated sounds from the 50s through to the futuristic \\"I Feel Love\\") to a groovy backdrop before beautifully morphing into ornate Disco reminiscent of Cerrone.<br /><br />The sound is far off from what everyone from David Guetta, Calvin Harris, or Skrillex are churning out. \\"Give Life Back To Music\\" is the opening cut and does what the title says, a robotic voice intoning against a groovy Chic-style retro groove, flying in the face of the anonymous mechanical Electronic Dance music currently cluttering up the charts.<br /><br />\\"Instant Crush\\" features Julian Casablancas dreamy elfin vocals against a chugging rock-ish arrangement. Lose Yourself To Dance\\" takes the tempo down a wee bit and features the vocals of Pharrell, who also sings on the breezy smash hit lead-single \\"Get Lucky\\". \\"Fragments Of Time\\" features Todd Edwards singing to a sunny 70s/80s Pop backdrop, while \\"Doin' It Right\\" is a spare robotic ballad featuring Panda Bear.<br /><br />\\"Within\\" is a stunning piano ballad with a winsome robotic voice singing \\"There are so many things that I don't understand...\\" which recalls Radiohead. \\"Touch\\" is an ambitious tempo-shifting piece with groovy bass, darting horns, and the vocals of Paul Williams, a maelstrom of instrumentation and a masterpiece! \\"Beyond\\" is an incredibly beautiful mid tempo trippy groove. Similar is \\"The Game Of Love\\".<br /><br />For those that enjoy their instrumental pieces, there's the swirling \\"Motherboard\\" (with interesting percussion patterns), and \\"Contact\\" (which starts off with the real-life recording of astronaut Eugene Cernan's narration of a UFO sighting).<br /><br />Daft Punk take you on an exhilarating ride, one of the best you'll get this year.oard\\" (with interesting percussion patterns), and \\"Contact\\" (which starts off with the real-life recording of astronaut Eugene Cernan's narration of a UFO sighting).<br /><br />Daft Punk take you on an exhilarating ride, one of the best you'll get this year.

But can it all be traced back to Mr. Clarke and this story from 1968? Is Mr. Clarke the one to blame for Matrix Revolutions and Terminator III and IV?), the tumbling adventure through the Star Gate, the \\"star child\\" and the return to Earth.<br /><br />The theme that struck most for me was that of evolution:<br /><br />\\"There were other thinkers, Bowman also found, who held even more exotic views. They did not believe that really advanced beings would possess organic bodies at all. Sooner or later, as their scientific knowledge progressed, they would get rid of the fragile, disease-and-accident-prone homes that Nature had given them, and which doomed them to inevitable death. They would replace their natural bodies as they wore out-- or perhaps even before that-- by constructions of metal and plastic, and would thus achieve immortality. The brain might linger for a little while as the last remnant of the organic body, directing its mechanical limbs and observing the universe through its electronic senses-- senses far finer and subtler than those that blind evolution could ever develop.<br /><br />\\"Even on Earth, the first steps in this direction had been taken. There were millions of men, doomed in earlier ages, who now lived active and happy lives thanks to artificial limbs, kidneys, lungs, and hearts. To this process there could be only one conclusion-- however far off it might be. And eventually even the brain might go. As the seat of consciousness, it was not essential; the development of electronic intelligence had proved that. The conflict between mind and machine might be resolved at last in the eternal truce of complete symbiosis...<br /><br />\\"But was even this the end? A few mystically inclined biologists went still further. They speculated, taking their cues from the beliefs of many religions, that mind would eventually free itself from matter. The robot body, like the flesh-and-blood one, would be no more than a stepping-stone to something which, long ago, men had called \\"spirit.\\" And if there was anything beyond that, its name could only be God.\\"<br /><br />The bottom line: Although \\"2001: A Space Odyssey\\" is an easy read, there isn't enough time in a review such as this to delve into its varied and important messages and meanings. Mr. Clarke's admonition seems to be that humans are evolving, improving as we had millions of years ago to this day and the future will likely be more of the same (advancement and war), foreshadowed with this nugget of repetitive prose (from the Moon-Watcher to the Star Child):<br /><br />\\"Then he waited, marshaling his thoughts and brooding over his still untested powers. For though he was master of the world, he was not quite sure what to do next.<br /><br />\\"But he would think of something.\\"<br /><br />-Raeden Zenow lived active and happy lives thanks to artificial limbs, kidneys, lungs, and hearts. B00BAYLQI0|4.0|THE IMPOSSIBLE takes us deep into a true nightmare that few have experienced or survived. It is an unnervingly realistic account of one family's dispair and impossible survival despite all odds.<br />English/Scottish couple Maria and Henry (Naomi Watts and Ewan McGregor) and their three young boys have made the fateful decision to holiday in beautiful Thailand over Christmas. No one could have been prepared for the horrors of a tsunami turning miles of lush, beautiful countryside into a disaster zone.<br /><br />The amazing realism of the tsunami and the sense of what it is like to be pulled under the water as tons of debris swirl around you is made very clear in THE IMPOSSIBLE. The realism pulls you into its own tsunami as seconds seem to last for hours. The constant movement of debris and of human beings in the churning violent water can be too much to bear at times but this is realism at its finest.<br /><br />Here is one family's story. It's just one of countless stories that may never be told. It's even more a story of a mother and her son as they fight for survival and eventually hope to be reunited with the rest of their family. This is the true story of Maria Belon and her family. Ironically, the real Spanish family is now English/Scottish and their names (except for Maria's) are now anglicized.<br /><br />There are amazing performances by newcomer Tom Holland (as oldest son Lucas)and Watts and McGregor. Watts brings us the pain and despair of the real Maria in her desperate struggle for life and to reunite her family. It's an amazing journey into the love and faith of one family. THE IMPOSSIBLE focuses on one family and there has been some criticism of that fact, yet their story is just one piece of an enormous puzzle. Maria Belon seriously promoted her story and survival so nothing is being given away by knowing this is a story of one family's survival.<br /><br />There is a human interest story here of how people from different nationalities come togetherin a tragedy. There is only a brief interaction with an uninjured couple upset about the inconvenience of not being able to quickly book a flight home. How many people reacted that way? It's a subject for another film.<br /><br />The scenes of the tsunami are beyond incredible and the depiction of compassion and kindess are heartwarming. A mother's love for her son is so clear through Watts's performance and the sadness of a young boy suddenly having to become a man is tough. THE IMPOSSIBLE slows down as Watts is in the hospital but then we pick up Henry's story with the two younger sons. Neither half of the separated family knows the fate of the other. No family should ever be in that situation.<br /><br />THE IMPOSSIBLE will upset and unnerve some simply because of its realistic depiction of the world's biggest recorded tsunami. Watts and McGregor prove they are world class actors and young Tom Holland is an amazing newcomer with all the emotions of a boy forced into manhood. Overall, THE IMPOSSIBLE is an amazing film.

B001ANSSDC|5.0|After hearing so many friends rave about the movie, Silver Linings Playbook, I decided to read the book before watching the DVD.  Written by Matthew Quick, I can't say enough good things about this novel.  It was funny, it was sad, it was moving, it was uplifting and it was eye-opening.  As since it takes place very close to where I live, I thoroughly enjoyed all the local references.  Author Quick also shines a much-needed light on bi-polar disorder, although it is never identified as such in the book.<br /><br />Silver Linings Playbook opens as Pat Peoples is checked out of a mental health facility in Baltimore by his mom, who takes him to his childhood home in Collingswood, NJ.  Pat had a violent incident four years prior, and that episode caused him to lose his wife, his house, his car, his career, and his freedom.  He has little memory of that event, but he's determined to set out on a path of self-improvement to win back his beloved Nikki.  Pat believes that his life is a movie and he is always searching for the silver lining.  He wants a happy ending.  Pat's mom is a kind and nurturing soul, but his father is aloof and most incommunicative.  But the entire family rallies around the Eagles during the NFL season.  This is the glue that starts to bond father and son, although it is a tenuous bond, at best.  Pat's best friend Ronnie has a recently widowed sister-in-law, Tiffany, who is another wounded soul in therapy and taking meds.  Pat and Tiffany are fixed up, but without much success at first.  But Tiffany offers Pat a deal--if he will join her in a dance competition, she will help him with something very important.  One of her demands is that Pat have nothing to do with football until the competition is over.  How this plays out is quite funny at times, but also moving and sad.<br /><br />Silver Linings Playbook is told in the first person, and Pat Peoples lets the reader in on his tortured world.  In comparing himself to his brother Jake, Jake \\"is not trying to improve his life at all, because he doesn't ever feel the war that goes on in my chest every single (f) day--the chemical explosives that light up my skull like the Fourth of July and the awful needs and impulses and...\\"  But Pat also has a keen insight when dealing with Tiffany.  \\"She looks sad.  She looks angry.  She looks different from everyone else I know--she cannot put on that happy face others wear when they know they are being watched.  She doesn't put on a face for me, which makes me trust her somehow.\\"<br /><br />Some of the funniest scenes involve the 2008 Eagles' season.  Quick shows it all including the rabid fans who hate the Redskins, the Giants, and especially, the Dallas Cowboys.  We see the superstitions, the rituals, the elaborate tailgate parties (the green football carnival), the fights, the wins, the losses, and the injured players.  There are also high hopes and dashed dreams--as with most professional sports teams.
